  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c1ca40e6-32e6-42e9-911d-48d92bdecc46'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer10533827616089264608">If Thursday thought she could avoid the spotlight after her heroic escapades in the pages of Jane Eyre, she was sorely mistaken.   <span id="freeText10533827616089264608" style="display:none">If Thursday thought she could avoid the spotlight after her heroic escapades in the pages of Jane Eyre, she was sorely mistaken. The unforgettable literary detective whom Michiko Kakutani of The New York Times calls "part Bridget Jones, part Nancy Drew and part Dirty Harry" had another think coming. The love of her life has been eradicated by Goliath, everyone's favorite corrupt multinational. To rescue him Thursday must retrieve a supposedly vanquished enemy from the pages of "The Raven." But Poe is off-limits to even the most seasoned literary interloper. Enter a professional: the man-hating Miss Havisham from Dickens's Great Expectations. As her new apprentice, Thursday keeps her motives secret as she learns the ropes of Jurisfiction, where she moonlights as a Prose Resource Operative inside books. As if jumping into the likes of Kafka, Austen, and Beatrix Potter's Tale of the Flopsy Bunnies weren't enough, Thursday finds herself the target of a series of potentially lethal coincidences, the authenticator of a newly discovered play by the Bard himself, and the only one who can prevent an unidentifiable pink sludge from engulfing all life on Earth.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10533827616089264608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

(October 1853 to February 1856)<br />In short, yes. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2319544530" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2319544530" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2319544530?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=fforde-jasper">fforde-jasper</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2319544530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2409795152179283340">The idea of parallel universes, alternate timelines, uchronias,… is an often used trope, but in this constellation and with the interconnections and dependencies on and in the real book world and the not any more so just fictional second world, it gives the idea a whole new dimension.<br/><br/>It´s close to a literary and sociological experiment to integrate the worldview, mentality, history, of the time the novels were created and how they influenced the awareness about those times and how novels are mor</span>
  <span id="freeText2409795152179283340" style="display:none">The idea of parallel universes, alternate timelines, uchronias,… is an often used trope, but in this constellation and with the interconnections and dependencies on and in the real book world and the not any more so just fictional second world, it gives the idea a whole new dimension.<br /><br />It´s close to a literary and sociological experiment to integrate the worldview, mentality, history, of the time the novels were created and how they influenced the awareness about those times and how novels are more than just entertainment, but studies about different times of human history, of changing morality, genre pictures, true crime history distilled on pages.<br /><br />The authors´ influence reaches a whole new dimension if one sees fictional works not just as something existing in the writers and readers mind, but as real and true worldbuilding, a kind of superpower to construct new worlds, the ultimate mind over matter proof, the option to be a creator of fictional universes for everybody.<br /><br />Time travel, split up personalities that could develop in different directions, criticism of cartels, one world trying to take over the other, exaggeration of many character tropes, evil powers trying to destroy one of the worlds or subjects in it,… there is so much hidden in this universe that it´s difficult to get it all in just one read. It´s one of the greatest love letters to reading and literature in general too.<br /><br />I imagine that a series like this could go on close to forever because the options are on the table and there is not just all literature ever written, but everything published this day, not to mention new forms of art such as video games and the good old buddies movies and series that are now having a renaissance thanks to VR and AR. An expanded satire universe like this would be something I want to totally get lost in. <br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Creator/JasperFforde">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/ThursdayNext">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2409795152179283340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_258125279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258125279" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7365405-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522094190p2/7365405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258125279?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/7365405-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=1-fiction">1-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=2-fic-fantasy-and-scifi">2-fic-fantasy-and-scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=3-multi-book-series">3-multi-book-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258125279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7019458287707314869"><b>
  <i>
    <u>Book Review</u>
  </i>
</b><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4432.Jasper_Fforde' title='Jasper Fforde' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jasper Fforde</a> had a stroke of brilliance with the "Thursday Next" series of adventure books. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1408889.Lost_in_a_Good_Book__Thursday_Next___2_' title='Lost in a Good Book (Thursday Next, #2) by Jasper Fforde' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lost in a Good Book</a> is the second release in the series and I've given it a very high 3 of 5 stars. As it's a very difficult book to truly wrap your head around, it couldn't get a 5 from me. When I compared it to the first one, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2019737.The_Eyre_Affair__Thursday_Next___1_' title='The Eyre Affair (Thursday Next, #1) by Jasper Fforde' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Eyre Affair</a>, I had to give it a slightly lower rating just because I enjoyed the first one more. A few really cool things about these books:<br/><br/>1. Thursday </span>
  <span id="freeText7019458287707314869" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <u>Book Review</u>
  </i>
</b><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4432.Jasper_Fforde" title="Jasper Fforde" rel="nofollow noopener">Jasper Fforde</a> had a stroke of brilliance with the "Thursday Next" series of adventure books. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1408889.Lost_in_a_Good_Book__Thursday_Next___2_" title="Lost in a Good Book (Thursday Next, #2) by Jasper Fforde" rel="nofollow noopener">Lost in a Good Book</a> is the second release in the series and I've given it a very high 3 of 5 stars. As it's a very difficult book to truly wrap your head around, it couldn't get a 5 from me. When I compared it to the first one, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2019737.The_Eyre_Affair__Thursday_Next___1_" title="The Eyre Affair (Thursday Next, #1) by Jasper Fforde" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eyre Affair</a>, I had to give it a slightly lower rating just because I enjoyed the first one more. A few really cool things about these books:<br /><br />1. Thursday is a literary detective who can jump into a book to try to solve whatever crime has occurred within the book.<br /><br />2. Crimes can include changing plot lines, removing characters, introducing chaos...<br /><br />3. You have to be mad or brilliant, or both, to come up with these kinds of stores. In this one, "The Raven" and "Flopsy Bunny" are major character arcs. Can you imagine dealing with that?<br /><br />4. The book has footnotes on every page, but they're not real footnotes. They are commentary or thoughts about what's being said in the book that the person talking wouldn't necessarily know, but the reader needs to know them. I'm sure you're confused if you've never read one of these books. So am I from time to time, and I've read three of them.<br /><br />5. It's such a great concept, and sometimes well-executed. And it's got your typical romance component in it too.<br /><br />6. But it can get very confusing if you don't read slowly and think about every single action. There are so many made up words, actions, histories... it's an alternative fantasy universe and you never know what might actually happen.<br /><br />7. At times, I think it's one of the best stories I've read. At others, it's still confusing me. But I focus on the little parts surrounding the realities of the characters and what they are doing.<br /><br />Phew.... complicated to write this review. It can't be a normal one without it going on for pages about what is actually going on. All you need to know is if you have a huge imagination, don't need structure, and love books... you must give it a chance.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>About Me</u>
  </i>
</b><br />For those new to me or my reviews... here's the scoop: I read A LOT. I write A LOT. And now I blog A LOT. First the book review goes on Goodreads, and then I send it on over to my WordPress blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://thisismytruthnow.com">https://thisismytruthnow.com</a>, where you'll also find TV &amp; Film reviews, the revealing and introspective 365 Daily Challenge and lots of blogging about places I've visited all over the world. And you can find all my social media profiles to get the details on the who/what/when/where and my pictures. Leave a comment and let me know what you think. Vote in the poll and ratings. Thanks for stopping by. <i>Note</i>: All written content is my original creation and copyrighted to me, but the graphics and images were linked from other sites and belong to them. Many thanks to their original creators.<br /><br />[polldaddy poll=9729544]	<br /><br />[polldaddy poll=9719251]</span>

<div id="review_131178553" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131178553" />
    <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon"><img alt="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572581488p2/1209800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131178553?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=historical-fantasy">historical-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131178553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8393248917570650382">This is one of those books that I wanted to like so much more than I did. Hell, it's one of those books that I feel like I <i>should</i> like more than I do. I mean, with the little literary cameos and the wry humor (and occasionally groan-inducing puns), with the jumping through books and really just the whole thing - it should be right up my alley. But it just doesn't work for me.<br/><br/>Part of it is that I feel it has a little bit of the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68496.Un_Lun_Dun' title='Un Lun Dun by China Miéville' rel='nofollow noopener'>Un Lun Dun</a> problem - it seems more a showcase for all the nifty ideas</span>
  <span id="freeText8393248917570650382" style="display:none">This is one of those books that I wanted to like so much more than I did. Hell, it's one of those books that I feel like I <i>should</i> like more than I do. I mean, with the little literary cameos and the wry humor (and occasionally groan-inducing puns), with the jumping through books and really just the whole thing - it should be right up my alley. But it just doesn't work for me.<br /><br />Part of it is that I feel it has a little bit of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68496.Un_Lun_Dun" title="Un Lun Dun by China Miéville" rel="nofollow noopener">Un Lun Dun</a> problem - it seems more a showcase for all the nifty ideas and wordplay that Fforde can throw in, but he seems less concerned with developing interesting and/or likable characters and an actual plot line with any sort of momentum.<br /><br />And part of it is that while I really like the idea of Jurisfiction and it seems like a really cool premise, I'm less enthralled with the execution. Parts of it just don't make sense. For instance, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the characters in the books are limited to their lines and actions in the book, and, when someone is reading their book, they have to be there to say their lines'; however, these same characters often go gallivanting into other books and doing various business for Jurisfiction. So what happens when someone reads one of their books when they're not there?<br /><br />I mean, sometimes they have a character exchange program, but that seems to be for more long term things. For short term cases, it just seems like they aren't in their books. So who takes over if they're not there?<br /><br />And I'm unclear on whether the characters that come out of the book are for specific editions, or, since the library at Jurisfiction is sort of an place of archetypes - where the books are alive - if a character is removed from one edition, are they removed from all editions?<br /><br />And, if so, how come throwing Jack Schitt into the Raven only seemed to effect the version that Thursday was reading? Or was it all versions, and, if it was all versions, then why was no one mad at her for that when they were mad at her for 'changing' the ending of Jane Eyre? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And maybe there are answers to all these issues, and I just don't care enough to remember them. Or whatever.<br /><br />There were some things I liked. As I said, I do enjoy some of the puns and wordplay (even if some of it's a bit, erm, low-brow. I mean, I'm ok with low-brow, but it's a little bit said when characters with the names of Schitt-Hause and Mr. Dedman and Mr. Walken are the height of humor.)<br /><br />And I did like the bits with Mycroft. He's still my favorite character, I think.<br /><br />Anyway - these books came highly recommended from a trusted source, and they really do seem like they should be something I should enjoy far more than I do, and I wanted to be able to give it at least a 3 star rating, but when about 3/4 of the way through I realized I just wanted it to be over already, I realized that I just couldn't.<br /><br />And so... I don't know if I'll continue with the series or not. If I do I'll definitely be getting it from the library.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8393248917570650382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1805181983" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1805181983" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1805181983?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781565117570" href="/book/show/535175.Lost_in_a_Good_Book">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1audio">1audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=3series">3series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1805181983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2160156818896836769">Maybe only a 3.5 star, but it was another fun trip into such a strange world filled with literary references, slippery characters, murder, & mayhem. There's plenty of wry humor, puns, & ridiculous situations to make sure things don't get too serious. I'd call it a cozy mystery, except that belies just how fantastic the world is & there is no way the reader can figure out what is going to happen. I sometimes wonder if the author knows. He writes the way Mrs. Haversham (Yes, the lady from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2623.Great_Expectations' title='Great Expectations by Charles Dickens' rel='nofollow noopener'>Great Ex</a></span>
  <span id="freeText2160156818896836769" style="display:none">Maybe only a 3.5 star, but it was another fun trip into such a strange world filled with literary references, slippery characters, murder, &amp; mayhem. There's plenty of wry humor, puns, &amp; ridiculous situations to make sure things don't get too serious. I'd call it a cozy mystery, except that belies just how fantastic the world is &amp; there is no way the reader can figure out what is going to happen. I sometimes wonder if the author knows. He writes the way Mrs. Haversham (Yes, the lady from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2623.Great_Expectations" title="Great Expectations by Charles Dickens" rel="nofollow noopener">Great Expectations</a>.) drives - with complete abandon &amp; sheer joy. 'It's a mixed up, muddled up, shook up world except for <s>Lola</s> Thursday. Oh, oh, <s>Lola</s> Thursday...' OK, I'll quit singing now, but if this series had a theme song, that wouldn't be a bad one.<br /><br />It was a bit uneven, but I put that down to the high points striking me as so funny. There's a great scene at a book sale, for instance. I didn't quit chuckling for several minutes. Reminded me of the time I stood in line at 5am in 20 degree darkness to get Ghost Buster backpacks for the boys for Xmas. That was 30 years ago, so I can laugh about it now. The savagery of mostly mothers on the prowl was shocking &amp; a lot of fun to watch, once I got the backpacks, of course. <br /><br />Very well narrated which added to the atmosphere. I'm definitely up for another at some point. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2160156818896836769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5757169496600592593">Curses! About 40 pages from the end, I had to run out and get the next book in the Thursday Next series, "Well of Lost Plots." This book doesn't have an ending! Even worse, I got sucked up into it and had to keep going. <br/><br/>"Lost in a Good Book" is the sequel to "The Eyre Affair" starring spec ops officer Thursday Next. To say that Thursday's life is complicated is an understatement. I'm not going to get into the plot or characters of this book. To do so would spoil this book, the preceding book, an</span>
  <span id="freeText5757169496600592593" style="display:none">Curses! About 40 pages from the end, I had to run out and get the next book in the Thursday Next series, "Well of Lost Plots." This book doesn't have an ending! Even worse, I got sucked up into it and had to keep going. <br /><br />"Lost in a Good Book" is the sequel to "The Eyre Affair" starring spec ops officer Thursday Next. To say that Thursday's life is complicated is an understatement. I'm not going to get into the plot or characters of this book. To do so would spoil this book, the preceding book, and the following book. I will say that, unlike "The Eyre Affair", "Lost in a Good Book" does not stand on its own. You must have read the first book to understand it. Then, you will have to read the next book to get any resolution. (I rather suspect that there won't be any resolution in the next book either.)<br /><br />Now, I rarely read series. It's even more rare for me to read books in a series back to back. But, Jasper Fford is such a compelling writer with such a weird imagination, that I'm breaking my usual rules.<br /><br />If you like weirdness and literature, and don't mind spending a lot of time on a series, go ahead and read the Thursday Next series. They are a lot of fun.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1548287788" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1548287788" />
    <a title="Kath ❅" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51266245-kath"><img alt="Kath ❅" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457893903p2/51266245.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1548287788?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kath ❅" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kath ❅" href="/user/show/51266245-kath">Kath ❅</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51266245-kath?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51266245-kath?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51266245-kath?shelf=read-but-dont-own">read-but-dont-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1548287788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16786034913977969484">I really, really liked this sequel! I liked the first book in this series but I thought this one was incredible. I felt like this one really drove home the bookish element to this series that the first one only touched on. Some of my favorite parts about this book was the book jumping, the conversations in the footnotes, all the bootstrap paradoxes, and this books funny self awareness. In the last book we got a glimpse of Thursdays power to jump into the events of any book, but it wasn't the mai</span>
  <span id="freeText16786034913977969484" style="display:none">I really, really liked this sequel! I liked the first book in this series but I thought this one was incredible. I felt like this one really drove home the bookish element to this series that the first one only touched on. Some of my favorite parts about this book was the book jumping, the conversations in the footnotes, all the bootstrap paradoxes, and this books funny self awareness. In the last book we got a glimpse of Thursdays power to jump into the events of any book, but it wasn't the main plot line. In this book we really get to see how it all worked and I loved the imagery of a library that contains every book ever written as well as every idea for a book. I would love to just go hang out there for a while. I really liked the way the characters developed in this book. Last book I found the characters to be interesting but they didn't really grab me and I was way more interested in the alternate world the author created and not so much the characters. In this sequel I loved all the characters just as much as I loved the world building. I also enjoyed the mystery of this book a little more than the last one and I like seeing the Goliath Corporation take more of a front seat as the villain of these stories. Speaking of Goliath, my book had a little approval rating at the front of the book from Goliath which I thought was really cute and I love when books have those sort of things in them. I also loved how there were parts of this book that tied it to the titles of the previous books and to the sequels. And on top of that any book is made better in my mind with quotes at the beginnings of chapters. I loved this book a lot and to be honest I was a little surprised at that because the first one to me was good but not great. This book definitely convinced me to pick up the next book in this serious and I would enchorage anyone who read the the first book and liked the concept but thought some of the delivery was only meh, to definitely try this one because I think this one is a great sequel and a great improvement over the first one and I hope I like the next detective Next book as much as I liked this one! </span>
  <a data-text-id="16786034913977969484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/244169295?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petra" href="/user/show/1733683-petra">Petra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13715649412618020794">September, 2020:<br/>I listened to the audio of this book to refresh my memory before continuing with the series.<br/>This is still a story that is a lot of fun to read. There are so many clever & interesting oddities in Thursday's world. It's fresh and very entertaining. <br/>I enjoyed this story more than the first book (which I liked). I think it's because I got to know the characters more, they became more real. Their world was more familiar and the story was touching. <br/>I look forward to continuing with Thu</span>
  <span id="freeText13715649412618020794" style="display:none">September, 2020:<br />I listened to the audio of this book to refresh my memory before continuing with the series.<br />This is still a story that is a lot of fun to read. There are so many clever &amp; interesting oddities in Thursday's world. It's fresh and very entertaining. <br />I enjoyed this story more than the first book (which I liked). I think it's because I got to know the characters more, they became more real. Their world was more familiar and the story was touching. <br />I look forward to continuing with Thursday's story (I would still like to have a Dodo).<br /><br />Jan, 2012:<br />A helluva lot of fun. I didn’t mean to read this book right now. Having been rather lukewarm about the first book in this series, I wasn’t sure whether to continue but some have said the series gets better. I thought I'd scan the first few pages and decide what to do.<br />Then, like Thursday Next, I fell into this book. It was clever, delightful; entertaining with lots of plot twists and turns, including an end-of-the-world scenario. <br />Miss Havisham is interesting. She’s assertive, in charge, smart and resourceful. I wonder what Dickens would think of Fforde's rendition of his stern, revengeful character.<br />I’m looking forward to the rest of this series now. Fforde has an amazing imagination. <br />I also want a Dodo. Plock-Plock.</span>

<div id="review_1368874931" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1368874931" />
    <a title="BrokenTune" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10592271-brokentune"><img alt="BrokenTune" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391017756p2/10592271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1368874931?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BrokenTune" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BrokenTune" href="/user/show/10592271-brokentune">BrokenTune</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/828364.Lost_in_a_Good_Book">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10592271-brokentune?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1368874931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3086438765884236981"><i>‘Bad boy!’ she added in a scolding tone. The Tasmanian tiger looked crestfallen, sat on its blanket by the Aga and stared down at its paws. ‘Rescue Thylacine,’ explained my mother. ‘Used to be a lab animal. He smoked forty a day until his escape. It’s costing me a fortune in nicotine patches. Isn’t it, DH-82?’</i><br/> <br/>This is such a clever book and there ere are so many quotable passages, but the problem is that may favourite parts contain spoilers of either this book or of pretty much any classic work </span>
  <span id="freeText3086438765884236981" style="display:none"><i>‘Bad boy!’ she added in a scolding tone. The Tasmanian tiger looked crestfallen, sat on its blanket by the Aga and stared down at its paws. ‘Rescue Thylacine,’ explained my mother. ‘Used to be a lab animal. He smoked forty a day until his escape. It’s costing me a fortune in nicotine patches. Isn’t it, DH-82?’</i><br /> <br />This is such a clever book and there ere are so many quotable passages, but the problem is that may favourite parts contain spoilers of either this book or of pretty much any classic work of literature worth reading. <br /> <br />I really admire the level of detail and research that Fforde put into this book, but I didn't think it lived up to the enjoyment of the first book, The Eyre Affair, tho. Maybe the novelty of Thursday's world has worn off a bit already, maybe the incessant puns and jokes were just a bit too much.<br /> <br />However, Thursday is still one of the best protagonists out there - kickass and kind.<br /> <br />The only real problem I have with this book is that it was so obviously written with the idea to continue the story in book #3 and therefore doesn't even attempt to be a standalone story - which makes me feel somewhat cheated and tricked into having to get the next book to find out what happened to my favourite characters.<br /> <br />I NEED TO KNOW THAT THE EGG IS OK!<br /> <br />Seriously, not cool, Mr. Fforde. But I guess, now I know how Scott's or Dickens' readers must have felt when they had to wait for the next installments of their stories.<br /> <br />And, yeah, I obviously am still in denial that Harry Potter worked the same way - except that I wanted to read the other books for their own sake, not to find out what happened to one particular character.<br /> <br />Ugh. <br /><br />(Changed my mind about the rating and going to go with 3*, not 3.5*.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3086438765884236981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_17071876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17071876" />
    <a title="Lena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/220791-lena"><img alt="Lena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589815535p2/220791.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17071876?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lena" href="/user/show/220791-lena">Lena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/220791-lena?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17071876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12930396961265814349">Though I'm not generally a big fan of book series, the Thursday Next books are really growing on me. This second book picks up shortly after The Eyre Affair ended and follows Thursday as she again tangles with Goliath, tries to figure out why she is experiencing life-threatening coincidences, and begins to learn more about the fine art of book-jumping. <br/><br/>Though character development does not seem to be Fforde's priority and the bad guys in particular a little too thinly drawn, the underlying premi</span>
  <span id="freeText12930396961265814349" style="display:none">Though I'm not generally a big fan of book series, the Thursday Next books are really growing on me. This second book picks up shortly after The Eyre Affair ended and follows Thursday as she again tangles with Goliath, tries to figure out why she is experiencing life-threatening coincidences, and begins to learn more about the fine art of book-jumping. <br /><br />Though character development does not seem to be Fforde's priority and the bad guys in particular a little too thinly drawn, the underlying premise of this book was so interesting to me I was able to overlook the occasional clichéd moment. As someone who has always gotten easily lost in books, I really love the idea of being able to literally enter books and explore the world behind the story on the page. Fforde has created an endlessly interesting world of possibilities with his oddball alternate reality, and I am most curious to see where he will take it next.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12930396961265814349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_926197188" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/926197188" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/926197188?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780670031900" href="/book/show/77021.Lost_in_a_Good_Book">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who loves books</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Carmen by: </span>
      Library
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published">traditionally-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=he-says">he-says</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer926197188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12640075674894619260">This is the 2nd book in the series, after THE EYRE AFFAIR. Read that first, or you might be a bit lost.<br/><br/>Thursday Next is now married to Landon. They are so in love. Both veterans of the Crimean War, they have put the past behind them and started a new future together.<br/><br/>Thursday is a Special Operative. She is a LiteraTec, someone who deals with stolen and forged books. But Thursday is also blessed with a rare special power - she can travel INTO books.<br/><br/>In this book she visits, among others, Sense and </span>
  <span id="freeText12640075674894619260" style="display:none">This is the 2nd book in the series, after THE EYRE AFFAIR. Read that first, or you might be a bit lost.<br /><br />Thursday Next is now married to Landon. They are so in love. Both veterans of the Crimean War, they have put the past behind them and started a new future together.<br /><br />Thursday is a Special Operative. She is a LiteraTec, someone who deals with stolen and forged books. But Thursday is also blessed with a rare special power - she can travel INTO books.<br /><br />In this book she visits, among others, Sense and Sensibility, Great Expectations, The Raven, and. The Trial by Kafka.<br /><br />She lives in an alternate universe, one where every average Joe and Jane on the street has vast literary knowledge to rival one of our dimensions English Professors. People literally kill each other while arguing who Shakespeare REALLY was. Parents name their kids after famous authors, so, for example, there might be 2,000 or so women named Jane Austen in London, each with a tiny number after their name so that the government can keep track of them.<br /><br />Technology is also a bit different. People ride in dirigibles instead of jetliners. Extinct species are brought back to life (Thursday has a pet dodo named Pickwick, who is very cute). Neandrathals have been brought back and are now fighting for their rights (the government forced sterilization on all of them).<br /><br />Thursday herself is one of my favorite characters in a long time. She's about 35. She dresses frumpy, is a war veteran, is smart, witty, and world-weary. I really enjoy reading about her. She seems like a "real" woman to me. Fforde never even mentions her breasts or her body - ever. And Thursday never wastes her time thinking about men and love, except for her own husband, Landon. And that's a sweet and real relationship, not just a jealousy-fueled-sex fest. SO REFRESHING.<br /><br />I was so, so angry reading this book. I was in a state of rage. Those f*cking bastards from Goliath <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ eradicated her husband! They went back in time and killed him when he was two-years-old! I AM SO ANGRY!!! I literally had to take a break from reading. Poor Thursday. Only she even remembers that she was even married in the first place.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The only problem is that Thursday <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ is pregnant with Landon's baby! She really doesn't want the kid to grow up without a father, so she is determined to get Landon back.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I adore Thursday's sweet father, a time-traveler on the run from Special Ops, who cares about her and always shows up in the nick of time to help her and guide her. They have a great, sweet, father-daughter relationship. Aw.<br /><br />And her crazy, genius uncle Mycroft and patient aunt Polly. And her brother, Joff, who in this book is revealed to be a gay man. Just very casually. He doesn't conform to any "gay sterotypes." He's just a bloke who happens to like men. VERY REFRESHING, FFORDE.<br /><br />This book is for people who love books and love literature. If you are not familiar with the classics, a lot of the jokes and references will go right over your head. That being said, it is funny, witty, fantastical, and smart - like a mixture of Alice in Wonderland and Hitchhiker's Guide. It's more serious than Hitchhiker, though. The stakes are higher, and you actually get very anxious and angry when bad stuff happens to the characters you've come to care about.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12640075674894619260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167342150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14956470572149713745">Super fun for book geeks like me. Even if I am unfamiliar with some of the books and characters mentioned here, as in the first Thursday Next book, I had no problem laughing out loud on occassion and following the plot. Having read this after Christopher Moore's "You Suck!" it is interesting to note the different approaches to creating humorous situations. Moore relies rather heavily on teenage angst and sex jokes while Fforde borrows from the English tradition of word play, absurdism (is this e</span>
  <span id="freeText14956470572149713745" style="display:none">Super fun for book geeks like me. Even if I am unfamiliar with some of the books and characters mentioned here, as in the first Thursday Next book, I had no problem laughing out loud on occassion and following the plot. Having read this after Christopher Moore's "You Suck!" it is interesting to note the different approaches to creating humorous situations. Moore relies rather heavily on teenage angst and sex jokes while Fforde borrows from the English tradition of word play, absurdism (is this even a word?) in the manner of Lewis Carroll and Eugene Ionesco, plus a healthy dose of straight slapstick.<br /><br />One small peeve about this book is in the rather thin plot. We have here something in the manner of an episodic novel, with a string of loosely connected set pieces and an overall arch that doesn't advance much and is left to be resolved in a future book.<br /><br />But all is forgiven in the sheer exuberance of wrecking havoc on timeline continuity and of playing loose with established literary characters. So if you are interested in finding about tensionolists, entroscopes, bloopholes, mnemonomorphs, oozemosis and so on ... this is the place to come to. <br /><br />to give an exampleof the Next style:<br />"Time is the glue of the cosmos, Thursday, and it has to be eased apart ? try to force events and they end up whacking you on the frontal lobes like a cabbage from six paces."</span>
  <a data-text-id="14956470572149713745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_41082776" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41082776" />
    <a title="Lightreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1836077-lightreads"><img alt="Lightreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1230606449p2/1836077.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41082776?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lightreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lightreads" href="/user/show/1836077-lightreads">Lightreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=derivative-fiction">derivative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41082776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5924745962721614917">Sequel to The Eyre Affair. Literary Detective Thursday Next is dealing with her sudden fame, pregnancy, the eradication of her husband from the timeline in order to force her to work for megacorp Goliath by going into books, the thing where someone is trying to kill her, her training as a Jurisfiction (hee) agent to ensure the integrity of books, and the impending end of the world.<br/><br/>Weird, fun, metafictional. Thursday slides in and out of books and her brand of reality, and there are some great li</span>
  <span id="freeText5924745962721614917" style="display:none">Sequel to The Eyre Affair. Literary Detective Thursday Next is dealing with her sudden fame, pregnancy, the eradication of her husband from the timeline in order to force her to work for megacorp Goliath by going into books, the thing where someone is trying to kill her, her training as a Jurisfiction (hee) agent to ensure the integrity of books, and the impending end of the world.<br /><br />Weird, fun, metafictional. Thursday slides in and out of books and her brand of reality, and there are some great little touches like communication via textual footnotes between people in fiction and people in reality. Mostly, these books are a big conglomeration of “hey, isn’t this neat?” saved by the fact that actually, yes, most of the things really are pretty freaking neat (though I say again, WTF with the random vampire subplot?).<br /><br />I do want to say, though, that these books are a perfect exemplar of the ways our IP and copyright systems are broken. Thursday does her Jurisfiction apprenticeship with Miss Havisham, and every other “real” fictional character she interacts with is in the public domain. I should also point out that these characters are explicitly extra-textual, with lives and personas outside the pages of the books they hail from – Fforde’s Miss Havisham drives motorboats, enjoys high-speed chases, and wears running shoes. But Fforde’s publisher would never permit him to work in a character who isn’t in the public domain, as it would be economically prohibitive even just to use a well-known name, irregardless of the personality attached. Fforde, being no fool, likely knows better than to even try. And if that isn’t a chilling effect, I don’t know what is.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5924745962721614917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans"><img alt="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587115780p2/7298986.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/594538180?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans">✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101158111" href="/book/show/8252732-lost-in-a-good-book">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=ffordalicious">ffordalicious</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer594538180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15543223819549565760">I read Lost in a Good Book when it was first published but decided to read the whole series again before burying myself in its last instalment, The Woman Who Died a Lot.<br/><br/>I was a bit disappointed after reading The Eyre Affair for the second time (it wasn't as enjoyable as I remembered it) so I wasn't sure what to expect from Lost in a Good Book. Still, I shouldn't have worried as this is such a great read!<br/><br/>The book is packed with wild, hilarious ideas : Thursday Next becomes an apprentice to Miss H</span>
  <span id="freeText15543223819549565760" style="display:none">I read Lost in a Good Book when it was first published but decided to read the whole series again before burying myself in its last instalment, The Woman Who Died a Lot.<br /><br />I was a bit disappointed after reading The Eyre Affair for the second time (it wasn't as enjoyable as I remembered it) so I wasn't sure what to expect from Lost in a Good Book. Still, I shouldn't have worried as this is such a great read!<br /><br />The book is packed with wild, hilarious ideas : Thursday Next becomes an apprentice to Miss Havisham (from "Great Expectations" and incidentally a mad driver) in order to become a Jurisfiction Prose Resource Operative (agents whose job is to maintain the integrity of popular fiction), she is prosecuted in Kafka's "The Trial", someone tries to kill her through coincidences, there are grammasites that live inside books and feed on grammar, a Character Exchange Programme so that characters can vacation in a book other than the one they belong to, the Cheshire Cat is the librarian for The Great Library... These are only a few of the great ideas that make this book a fantastic read! Now on to read The Well of Lost Plots again :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15543223819549565760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_75490990" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75490990" />
    <a title="Sarah F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/327282-sarah-f"><img alt="Sarah F" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75490990?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah F" href="/user/show/327282-sarah-f">Sarah F</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75490990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer317403704637701040">Lost in a Good Book - what a title. Would I have been in such a situation! Sadly, I was not, and I really hated this book to begin with. Half a star rating at best. In fact, the only reason I finished it was so that I could give it a bad review. By the end, I was able to stomach it, which isn't much for praise. <br/><br/>I haven't much patience with books that try to be clever, and this book is dripping with unsupportable pretentiousness. For a long time, I thought the main character was a man, for this m</span>
  <span id="freeText317403704637701040" style="display:none">Lost in a Good Book - what a title. Would I have been in such a situation! Sadly, I was not, and I really hated this book to begin with. Half a star rating at best. In fact, the only reason I finished it was so that I could give it a bad review. By the end, I was able to stomach it, which isn't much for praise. <br /><br />I haven't much patience with books that try to be clever, and this book is dripping with unsupportable pretentiousness. For a long time, I thought the main character was a man, for this male author does not seem to have the ability to present a female character in a believable form. The world she inhabits is full of quirky characters who grated on me. The book is chock full of literary jokes and giggles, but again, the clever format in which they were presented took all the fun out of it. It was more like a small child saying, "See, look, I read books! I know plots! I know character names! Aren't I smart and well read??" A coworker gave me books two through four of this series, and I would really like to return them by throwing them at his head and asking how he can stand to read such garbage.</span>
  <a data-text-id="317403704637701040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1687296415182012286">While I didn’t feel quite the same extreme sense of glee about the final parts of the book as I did with the end the first book in the series (The Eyre Affair), the events toward the end of the book were, once again, exceedingly clever. And: I think that I enjoyed this book even more than the first one, which is saying a lot. I’m also thrilled because several people have told me that the next/third book in the series is their favorite so far; I believe that there are 5 now. I’m therefore very ea</span>
  <span id="freeText1687296415182012286" style="display:none">While I didn’t feel quite the same extreme sense of glee about the final parts of the book as I did with the end the first book in the series (The Eyre Affair), the events toward the end of the book were, once again, exceedingly clever. And: I think that I enjoyed this book even more than the first one, which is saying a lot. I’m also thrilled because several people have told me that the next/third book in the series is their favorite so far; I believe that there are 5 now. I’m therefore very eager to read the next book: The Well of Lost Plots. <br /><br />I’m finding that I am enjoying some books’ characters more in Fforde’s books than in their original books.<br /><br />Fforde is brilliant and these books are so much fun to read.<br /><br />I’m been strongly recommending this series to several friends. They might not be for everyone, but I’m so delighted that I found them, thanks to Goodreads. The books should be read in order, in my opinion; of course, I do think that about all series.<br /><br /></span>

        <a title="Gail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gail" href="/user/show/199326-gail">Gail</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12172913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15430414036057026448">A small disappointment after "The Eyre Affair". The hook or gimmick, that of an alternative reality where literature has a huge impact on humans' lives, apparently only holds up for one novel. I thought the first book was cute, innovative, and funny. Here the jokes became worn, the hook repetetive, and the characters just boxy and one-noted. <br/>The plot, which apparently is going to go on a la Harry Potter, involves Thursday trying to rescue her loved ones and herself. Just not very good, I'm afrai</span>
  <span id="freeText15430414036057026448" style="display:none">A small disappointment after "The Eyre Affair". The hook or gimmick, that of an alternative reality where literature has a huge impact on humans' lives, apparently only holds up for one novel. I thought the first book was cute, innovative, and funny. Here the jokes became worn, the hook repetetive, and the characters just boxy and one-noted. <br />The plot, which apparently is going to go on a la Harry Potter, involves Thursday trying to rescue her loved ones and herself. Just not very good, I'm afraid; I won't be reading another of these. And that's really too bad, because I was decieved by the first one's innovation into thinking it was actually a pretty good book. There are some great puns in the series, though.</span>

<div id="review_1522404111" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1522404111" />
    <a title="Jenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7206839-jenny"><img alt="Jenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593734236p2/7206839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1522404111?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny" href="/user/show/7206839-jenny">Jenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1522404111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14106959235964266332">I like The Eyre Affair better but only because it's slightly simpler. I love the allusions, but the plot has too many side plots going on. Sure, Fforde wraps them all up nicely, but it's a little convoluted for me. <br/>That being said, I love continuing with these characters and this world. Thursday is a great narrator, and the allusions are fun. I really enjoy the concept of this series, and the way the story moves forward is interesting and slightly unexpected. <br/>I recommend this book only to people</span>
  <span id="freeText14106959235964266332" style="display:none">I like The Eyre Affair better but only because it's slightly simpler. I love the allusions, but the plot has too many side plots going on. Sure, Fforde wraps them all up nicely, but it's a little convoluted for me. <br />That being said, I love continuing with these characters and this world. Thursday is a great narrator, and the allusions are fun. I really enjoy the concept of this series, and the way the story moves forward is interesting and slightly unexpected. <br />I recommend this book only to people who really liked The Eyre Affair. If you didn't like it much, you really won't like Lost in a Good Book, where everything distinctive about TEA becomes even more developed in this book. But if you like post-modern surrealist magical realistic science fiction fantasy, give this a shot.</span>

<div id="review_10915381" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10915381" />
    <a title="Skylar Burris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/710201-skylar-burris"><img alt="Skylar Burris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449959508p2/710201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/10915381?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skylar Burris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skylar Burris" href="/user/show/710201-skylar-burris">Skylar Burris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/710201-skylar-burris?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/710201-skylar-burris?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10915381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2044880180990741209">Although some of the novelty of Thursday Next's world has worn off by the time the reader reaches this sequel to The Eyre Affair, Fforde adds enough new treats to keep the book feeling almost as fresh as its prequel. The humour is as sharp as ever; indeed, Lost in a Good Book may be even funnier than Fforde's previous novel. The book is an easy read and is just fun. It narrates every bibliophile's childlike fantasy--the idea of being able to travel through books. There was one flaw in the work, </span>
  <span id="freeText2044880180990741209" style="display:none">Although some of the novelty of Thursday Next's world has worn off by the time the reader reaches this sequel to The Eyre Affair, Fforde adds enough new treats to keep the book feeling almost as fresh as its prequel. The humour is as sharp as ever; indeed, Lost in a Good Book may be even funnier than Fforde's previous novel. The book is an easy read and is just fun. It narrates every bibliophile's childlike fantasy--the idea of being able to travel through books. There was one flaw in the work, however, and that was the rather enigmatic climax, a world-saving event that did not make much sense to me. All in all, Lost in a Good Book is fantastic pleasure reading. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2044880180990741209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38534138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10461798670107570665">If you like reading, you will <i>love</i> Jasper Fforde's Thursday Next series. Set in an alternative history of England (and the world in general), where 27 levels of Special-Ops monitor everything and the mega-corporation Goliath is waiting to take over the world, it follows Thursday's adventures as a Litra-Tech apprentice of Miss Havisham of <u>Great Expectations</u> fame.<br/><br/>If you like books, spies and England and fantasy, this is a must read. Be sure to read <u>The Eyre Affair</u> first.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_5701346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5701346" />
    <a title="Tracey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/349264-tracey"><img alt="Tracey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1195243074p2/349264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5701346?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracey" href="/user/show/349264-tracey">Tracey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">mystery readers may be frustrated, but general bibliophiles should have a rollicking good time</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349264-tracey?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349264-tracey?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5701346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3576763976484553756">Previously read June 2004 - audiobook March 2012. <br/><br/>Checked out Lost in a Good Book after refreshing my memory of Thursday Next by re-reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27003.The_Eyre_Affair_Thursday_Next_1_' title='The Eyre Affair (Thursday Next, #1) by Jasper Fforde' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Eyre Affair</a>. [later purchased this]<br/><br/>The second book starts with Thursday as a semi-newlywed, continuing her work with SpecOps 27, the Literary Detectives Division. In between giving unwilling interviews, being harassed by Goliath and determining whether a newly-discovered play really was by Shakespeare, she is introduced to the Department of Jursifiction;</span>
  <span id="freeText3576763976484553756" style="display:none">Previously read June 2004 - audiobook March 2012. <br /><br />Checked out Lost in a Good Book after refreshing my memory of Thursday Next by re-reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27003.The_Eyre_Affair_Thursday_Next_1_" title="The Eyre Affair (Thursday Next, #1) by Jasper Fforde" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eyre Affair</a>. [later purchased this]<br /><br />The second book starts with Thursday as a semi-newlywed, continuing her work with SpecOps 27, the Literary Detectives Division. In between giving unwilling interviews, being harassed by Goliath and determining whether a newly-discovered play really was by Shakespeare, she is introduced to the Department of Jursifiction; run by those in the bookworld to make sure the stories stay straight. Several bizarre attempts on Thursday's life are made, Schitt-Hawse of Goliath teams up with her father's nemesis, Lavoisier to eradicate Thursday's husband...oh, and did I mention that a sibling of Acheron Hades makes an appearance? <br /><br />This installment of the Thursday Next series is a little more free-wheeling, with the multiple story threads weaving in and out (and sometimes getting tied in knots). The humour and literary in-jokes are as abundant as in the first book - though I wish the Library had been more how Borges described it. Dedicated mystery readers may be a little frustrated with the non-traditional plot, but general bibliophiles should have a rollicking good time.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3576763976484553756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48011177?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judy" href="/user/show/854592-judy">Judy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48011177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer385938202523282868">I'm in love with this series although I apear to be reading them out of order. This is the second in the series, and Thursday Next, who works as a Literary Dtective in Special Ops, has just her ground-breaking work in The Eyre Affair (she ended up changing the ending from Jane moving to India to Jane staying in England and marrying Mr. Rochester). Thursday is the talk of the town and Special Ops Public Relations wants her to do everything from television appearances (highly censored) to a possib</span>
  <span id="freeText385938202523282868" style="display:none">I'm in love with this series although I apear to be reading them out of order. This is the second in the series, and Thursday Next, who works as a Literary Dtective in Special Ops, has just her ground-breaking work in The Eyre Affair (she ended up changing the ending from Jane moving to India to Jane staying in England and marrying Mr. Rochester). Thursday is the talk of the town and Special Ops Public Relations wants her to do everything from television appearances (highly censored) to a possible work-out video. In this book which is full of puns and literary allusions, Thursday becomes a trainee of Miss Havisham from Great Expectations and ends up jumping into many well-loved books including Kafka's The Trial, Austen's Sense and Sensibility and Carroll's Alice in Wonderland (the Cheshire Cat runs the Great Library where all books every published are stored). Thursday runs afoul of Goliah Corporation by trapping of its executives, Jack Schitt, in Poe's The Raven. The adventures abound as Thursday tries to save the world from destruction, find her husband of four weeks who has been eradicated, and deal with the fluid boundaries between life and literature. A really fun read.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="385938202523282868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
